- **Changed files**: 2   **+254 / -0**

## Description

#### What type of PR is this?

/kind bug

#### What this PR does / why we need it:

It makes the --kubeconfig flag, when passed into the Kueue manager binary, respected by the visibility server.

This addresses https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/issues/8606.

#### Which issue(s) this PR fixes:
Fixes #8606 

#### Special notes for your reviewer:

#### Does this PR introduce a user-facing change?
```release-note
VisibilityOnDemand: Fix the bug that when running Kueue with the custom `--kubeconfig` flag the visibility server
fails to initialize, because the custom value of the flag is not propagated to it, leading to errors such as:
"Unable to create and start visibility server","error":"unable to apply VisibilityServerOptions: failed to get delegated authentication kubeconfig:  failed to get delegated authentication kubeconfig: ..."
```

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-05T10:46:14Z

Cool, regarding the e2e test, maybe we could use the [customconfig](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/tree/main/test/e2e/customconfigs) suite to pass the custom "kubeconfig" to Kueue in the deployment spec, restart, and verify it takes effect on the visibility server too, so it is used when serving requests to the endpoints, as a reference point for existing [visibility tests](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/singlecluster/visibility_test.go).

For example, here is the code  where we change temporarily configuration of the Kueue deployment for MultiKueue: [test code](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/multikueue/e2e_test.go#L1907-L1963)

### Comment by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-05T13:40:08Z

> Cool, regarding the e2e test, maybe we could use the [customconfig](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/tree/main/test/e2e/customconfigs) suite to pass the custom "kubeconfig" to Kueue in the deployment spec, restart, and verify it takes effect on the visibility server too, so it is used when serving requests to the endpoints, as a reference point for existing [visibility tests](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/singlecluster/visibility_test.go).
> 
> For example, here is the code where we change temporarily configuration of the Kueue deployment for MultiKueue: [test code](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/multikueue/e2e_test.go#L1907-L1963)

I understand what you would like to achieve, but there is one thing still unclear, how do you ensure that the visibility server ignores the fallback (in-cluster) configuration? I believe testing that the visibility server serves requests after the update in the deployment spec does not ensure that the config is not the one from the fallback `rest.InClusterConfig()`, right? So did you have in mind to provide a kubeconfig that points to a different mock server (not the real K8s API) and verify the traffic goes there? @mimowo

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-05T13:51:22Z

> So did you have in mind to provide a kubeconfig that points to a different mock server (not the real K8s API) and verify the traffic goes there? @mimowo

Yes, or basically embedding any executable code in the kubeconfig which would have side-effects which are detectable from the e2e test's perspective. IIRC there were some fields which allow to exec custom binary or call endpoint. Whatever is reasonably simple and works.

Then, in the e2e test code we could detect that when listing PendingWorkloads our server received a call (or if feasible the code could call kubectl to emit an event detectable by the e2e test code).

### Comment by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-05T16:01:36Z

> Yes, or basically embedding any executable code in the kubeconfig which would have side-effects which are detectable from the e2e test's perspective. IIRC there were some fields which allow to exec custom binary or call endpoint. Whatever is reasonably simple and works.
> 
> Then, in the e2e test code we could detect that when listing PendingWorkloads our server received a call (or if feasible the code could call kubectl to emit an event detectable by the e2e test code).

I noticed a practical problem with applying the `exec` plugin approach here: AFAIK Kueue’s images are distroless `(gcr.io/distroless/static:nonroot)`.

Because this is a distroless environment, the container lacks a shell (sh/bash), curl, kubectl, and basic GNU utilities. If we use the `exec` plugin in the kubeconfig, the client-go library will throw an `executable file not found in $PATH` error, causing the visibility server to crash before it can run any custom logic.

Maybe we could use some Negative Control followed by a Positive Control instead?

- The Negative Check: If the visibility server ignores the fallback in-cluster config and strictly uses our broken config, it will fail to perform the SubjectAccessReview (SAR) when we query it, and our E2E test will receive an `Unauthorized/Internal` error. This proves the flag overrides the default.

- The Positive Check: We then update the ConfigMap to a valid kubeconfig (pointing to `kubernetes.default.svc`), restart the pod, and verify the query succeeds. This proves the custom config actively works when correct.

Although, that does feel like an anti-pattern to be testing something that "fails" so I am not sure this is a very elegant approach... What do you think? @mimowo

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-05T16:08:49Z

> I noticed a practical problem with applying the exec plugin approach here: AFAIK Kueue’s images are distroless (gcr.io/distroless/static:nonroot).

I see, but we could mount some binary like kubectl similarly as we do [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/multikueue/e2e_test.go#L1907-L1963). I think @kshalot is pretty familiar with the code. This is particularly easy on 1.35+ which allows to mount any file from a container image.

> Maybe we could use some Negative Control followed by a Positive Control instead?
> (...)
> Although, that does feel like an anti-pattern to be testing something that "fails" so I am not sure this is a very elegant approach... What do you think? @mimowo

I'm ok with that for the first iteration, or if using the image proves tricky. Especially if you can test it works ok on a live cluster.

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-05T16:15:34Z

One idea would be to mount the agnhost image which we already use for testing (to avoid using too many random images). See docs: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/master/test/images/agnhost/README.md

One relatively simple idea is to use `entrypoint-tester`, call it with some string like "Hello World From Agnhost", and confirm the Kueue container logs contain the log line. wdyt?

I know this is pretty elaborate test for this... So I'm on the fence about the gain/effort. Still, if we are going about automated testing, I would suggest choosing this way.

### Comment by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-03-05T16:21:14Z

> I see, but we could mount some binary like kubectl similarly as we do [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/multikueue/e2e_test.go#L1907-L1963). I think @kshalot is pretty familiar with the code. This is particularly easy on 1.35+ which allows to mount any file from a container image.

I'll get back to this in a second, but I'm also thinking about alternatives... Since you can pass a user in the kubeconfig, maybe we could leverage RBAC here somehow? Maybe remove the permissions of the default Kueue SA, create a custom one for the test with the correct permissions and validate that it only works when you use that SA in the kubeconfig?

### Comment by [@dkaluza](https://github.com/dkaluza) — 2026-03-05T16:50:59Z

From my point of view mentioned RBAC scenario makes sense and probably shouldn't be too complex.

I had in mind also the following scenarios that might not be too hard and probably can check the functionality:
1. Have a regular cluster with kueue but disabled visibility server. 
2. Run just the visibility server outside the cluster  by calling  `visibility.CreateAndStartVisibilityServer` function.
3. Make a request for pending workloads and verify the returned values.

Or even whole Kueue can be run outside of the cluster as a regular docker image to check if it connects successfully. 

A separate service account can be a more regular and  production like use-case though

### Comment by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-05T16:59:24Z

> > I see, but we could mount some binary like kubectl similarly as we do [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/multikueue/e2e_test.go#L1907-L1963). I think @kshalot is pretty familiar with the code. This is particularly easy on 1.35+ which allows to mount any file from a container image.
> 
> I'll get back to this in a second, but I'm also thinking about alternatives... Since you can pass a user in the kubeconfig, maybe we could leverage RBAC here somehow? Maybe remove the permissions of the default Kueue SA, create a custom one for the test with the correct permissions and validate that it only works when you use that SA in the kubeconfig?

I think I like this approach best, and I believe we can reuse this idea of Negative and Positive Test as I mentioned earlier:

1. Create a Custom ServiceAccount and generate a token for it.
2. Mount the token and a custom KubeConfig pointing to that token into the visibility server.
3. Negative Test: Attempt to query the visibility server. Because our custom SA has no RBAC permissions, the request will fail (which proves it is using our custom SA and not falling back to the pod's default SA, which does have permissions).
4. Positive Test: Dynamically create the binding for our custom SA. The next query to the visibility server should succeed.

Do you think this is a valid approach?

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-05T16:59:33Z

> I had in mind also the following scenarios that might not be too hard and probably can check the functionality:

I'm not a fan of running the visibility server outside the cluster using `visibility.CreateAndStartVisibilityServer`. Given multiple back-and-forth about "where to put the flag extraction code", I would prefer to abstract-out how the visibility server is instantiated. Running the entire stack makes sure the code works ok no matter if the extraction is in main.go, or inside `visibility.CreateAndStartVisibilityServer`

### Comment by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-03-05T17:08:41Z

> 1. Create a Custom ServiceAccount and generate a token for it.
> 2. Mount the token and a custom KubeConfig pointing to that token into the visibility server.
> 3. Negative Test: Attempt to query the visibility server. Because our custom SA has no RBAC permissions, the request will fail (which proves it is using our custom SA and not falling back to the pod's default SA, which does have permissions).
> 4. Positive Test: Dynamically create the binding for our custom SA. The next query to the visibility server should succeed.

This makes sense to me. To be specific, apart from the visibility permissions I think we'll also need to add the `system:auth-delegator` role binding because the Kubeconfig will be injected into the authorization/authentication settings.

### Comment by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-06T09:58:08Z

Test is failing, please wait for fix before review.

### Comment by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-06T11:44:45Z

/test pull-kueue-test-e2e-customconfigs-main

### Comment by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-06T14:03:19Z

> > I see, but we could mount some binary like kubectl similarly as we do [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/test/e2e/multikueue/e2e_test.go#L1907-L1963). I think @kshalot is pretty familiar with the code. This is particularly easy on 1.35+ which allows to mount any file from a container image.
> 
> I'll get back to this in a second, but I'm also thinking about alternatives... Since you can pass a user in the kubeconfig, maybe we could leverage RBAC here somehow? Maybe remove the permissions of the default Kueue SA, create a custom one for the test with the correct permissions and validate that it only works when you use that SA in the kubeconfig?

This approach is proving to be flaky and overly complex..

To make the test work, the test suite has to dynamically clone the entire set of RoleBindings and ClusterRoleBindings from the default Kueue controller ServiceAccount to a custom test ServiceAccount. This is necessary so the controller manager can still boot up and function, while specifically omitting the `system:auth-delegator` permission to trigger the failure.

The test also relies on asserting that specific error types (like 401 Unauthorized, 403 Forbidden, or 503 Service Unavailable) are returned when the visibility server fails to perform a SubjectAccessReview. However, the exact error returned by the API server can vary based on timing (e.g., how quickly the kube-aggregator marks the service as unavailable) and the specific environment, leading to flaky test failures.

And to make things even more tricky, we have to introduce some timeout after dynamically binding `system:auth-delegator` as it can take a non-deterministic amount of time (sometimes up to a minute) for the aggregator to recognize the new permissions and allow the visibility server to perform SubjectAccessReview.

This feels overly complex for a test which only aim is to check that the visibility server spins up using the custom kubeconfig. I am considering moving towards the approach mentioned by @mimowo which uses the exec plugin in the kubeconfig to run a binary (like agnhost) that prints a unique string to the logs.

That way we can directly confirm that the visibility server is loaded and utilizes the provided kubeconfig file without the need for a Negative / Positive Test. If the binary runs, the flag works. Also checking for a specific log line is more deterministic and does not depend on the nuances of Kubernetes API error codes.

What do you think @kshalot ?

### Comment by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-03-06T14:30:17Z

I understand.

One obstacle that I foresee with the "exec" approach is that we'll have to correlate the execution with the visibility server, because I'm guessing it will be executed multiple times during setup (because the same kubeconfig is used in multiple places and not only by the visibility server). There's also caching involved - the credentials returned by `exec` will likely be cached until the token it returned expires. Hopefully this won't be the case here (because the auth config in visibility server gets a path, I'm hoping it will get its own "instance" of the kubeconfig and token).

FYI I'm not arguing against it, but just trying to think ahead. If the exec approach turns out to be simpler, then I'd say lets go for it.

### Comment by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-06T18:01:15Z

> I understand.
> 
> One obstacle that I foresee with the "exec" approach is that we'll have to correlate the execution with the visibility server, because I'm guessing it will be executed multiple times during setup (because the same kubeconfig is used in multiple places and not only by the visibility server). There's also caching involved - the credentials returned by `exec` will likely be cached until the token it returned expires. Hopefully this won't be the case here (because the auth config in visibility server gets a path, I'm hoping it will get its own "instance" of the kubeconfig and token).
> 
> FYI I'm not arguing against it, but just trying to think ahead. If the exec approach turns out to be simpler, then I'd say lets go for it.

I tried both ways and indeed the `exec` approach is also not as straight forward as I thought. In fact the RBAC approach is still "cleaner" and more robust in my opinion.

The test leverages `GetPendingWorkloadsSummary` and the list of expected errors is limited to `401/403/500/503`. Anything else should fail the test (for example we don't want a `404`).

When you have a moment, please review the changes @kshalot @dkaluza.

### Comment by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2026-03-11T19:01:43Z

/release-note-edit

```release-note
VisibilityOnDemand: Fix the bug that when running Kueue with the custom `--kubeconfig` flag the visibility server
fails to initialize, because the custom value of the flag is not propagated to it, leading to errors such as:
"Unable to create and start visibility server","error":"unable to apply VisibilityServerOptions: failed to get delegated authentication kubeconfig:  failed to get delegated authentication kubeconfig: ..."
```

## Reviews

### Review by [@dkaluza](https://github.com/dkaluza) (commented) — 2026-03-02T09:27:18Z

- **cmd/kueue/main.go:140** by [@dkaluza](https://github.com/dkaluza) — 2026-03-02T09:23:30Z
```diff
@@ -138,6 +136,11 @@ func main() {
 	zapOptions.BindFlags(flag.CommandLine)
 	flag.Parse()
 
+	var kubeConfigPath string
+	if kubeConfigFlag := flag.Lookup("kubeconfig"); kubeConfigFlag != nil {
```

  Aren't we handling this way only one particular flag?
  
  What about  the other flags? I know that the bug is about this one but if I understand correctly there are many more in the API server that might not work... And it would be best to have a more systematic approach. E.g. in this way one might still not be able to change the port of the API server, which is quite handy. 
  Sure we can be adding this one by one but I imagine there are many more flags than we wish to handle manually.
  
  Have you seen the discussion [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8761#issuecomment-3823888714)?

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-02T09:43:18Z

  > What about the other flags?
  
  Do we have some other flags which are required for the use-cases we know? If not, then we could separate the two problems:
  1. running the visibility server - as done in this PR. 
  2. Passing the other flags in the future (4.) in https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8761#issuecomment-3823888714
  
  Let me ask some questions regarding the (2.)  there.

### Review by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) (commented) — 2026-03-02T11:00:43Z

- **cmd/kueue/main.go:140** by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-02T11:00:43Z
```diff
@@ -138,6 +136,11 @@ func main() {

 	flag.Parse()
 
+	var kubeConfigPath string
+	if kubeConfigFlag := flag.Lookup("kubeconfig"); kubeConfigFlag != nil {
```

  Thanks for the feedback. For our use-case, we also need to pass a custom port for the visibility server. So the way I see it so far (but maybe there is another better solution), we can either:
  1. Replicate the same logic for custom port (something like [this](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/commit/0d3bf4c52e63d8fe14442e9776e8349f69f37d83))
  2. Convert all flags to `pflag` which as @olekzabl mentioned [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8761#issuecomment-3823888714) might introduce some undesirable side effects (hide behind a feature gate?)
  3. As @dkaluza mentioned [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8761#issuecomment-3824151822) we can separate the APIServer flags from the kueue core flags in some way
  
  What do you think?

### Review by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) (commented) — 2026-03-03T10:47:13Z

  From this [discussion](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8761#issuecomment-3983316307), I believe we can treat those concerns separately:
  
  1. Use a global --kubeconfig for the path (as is done in this PR)
  2. Use `--visibility-server-flags` for api server flags specific to Visibility Server (like custom port)

### Review by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) (commented) — 2026-03-04T11:00:04Z

- **pkg/visibility/server.go:117** by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-04T11:00:03Z

```diff
@@ -110,6 +110,10 @@ func applyVisibilityServerOptions(config *genericapiserver.RecommendedConfig, en

 	}

+		o.Authentication.RemoteKubeConfigFile = kubeConfigPath
```

  IIUC we don't need to specify the main kubeconfig path in the options because the server's ClientConfig is already explicitly initialized in `newVisibilityServerConfig` using the kubeConfig passed from [main.go](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/5d9e98e23f51d283da2a8f30571ff48bc391b1f1/cmd/kueue/main.go#L223C2-L223C37). 
  
  This way we make sure to preserve the custom settings (like the RateLimiter) applied in main. AFAIK the Authentication and Authorization options require the path specifically because they construct their own isolated clients, whereas the core server's client is already fully configured via the direct assignment. Or am I missing something?

### Review by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) (commented) — 2026-03-04T13:25:11Z

### Review by [@dkaluza](https://github.com/dkaluza) (commented) — 2026-03-04T13:29:00Z

- **pkg/visibility/server.go:117** by [@dkaluza](https://github.com/dkaluza) — 2026-03-04T13:29:00Z
```diff
@@ -110,6 +110,10 @@ func applyVisibilityServerOptions(config *genericapiserver.RecommendedConfig, en
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.CertFile = certDir + "/tls.crt"
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.KeyFile = certDir + "/tls.key"
 	}
+	if kubeConfigPath != "" {
+		o.Authentication.RemoteKubeConfigFile = kubeConfigPath
```

  I did some digging.
  
  I see, kubeconfig is assigned [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/main/pkg/visibility/server.go#L145) , where relevant documentation of apiserver says that this field is normally assigned by ApplyTo of options - [source](https://github.com/kubernetes/apiserver/blob/b4a095b3dc1ad68dd9a775f686fa1087612ef0cc/pkg/server/config.go#L343) - I'm not sure whether this is favorable approach - but shouldn't lead to problems as it was somehow working with default client. 
  
  On the other hand the auth clients are created like [this](https://github.com/kubernetes/apiserver/blob/b4a095b3dc1ad68dd9a775f686fa1087612ef0cc/pkg/server/options/authorization.go#L222). So if no config path is assigned in cluster-config will be used, or error will be raised - [sources](https://github.com/kubernetes/client-go/blob/master/rest/config.go#L543)
  And this is the error mentioned in issue.
  
  I'm currently not yet sure why those ENV VARS  are not assigned and why we need to pass the config. 
  
  Sure we can set those RemoteKubeConfigFile fields, but isn't the server anyway run in the cluster? From my point of view it would be good to understand the actual cause of the issue (which I currently do not understand) 
  
  Edit: Oh or the issue only occurs when actually running outside of the cluster? Then it looks like correct approach.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-04T13:43:17Z

- **cmd/kueue/main.go:142** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-04T13:43:17Z
```diff
@@ -138,6 +136,11 @@ func main() {
 	zapOptions.BindFlags(flag.CommandLine)
 	flag.Parse()
 
+	var kubeConfigPath string

+	}
```

  Silly question, but why do we do that in main.go? Cannot we just move the code where its result is needed - to `CreateAndStartVisibilityServer`

### Review by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) (commented) — 2026-03-04T13:57:15Z

- **pkg/visibility/server.go:117** by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-04T13:57:15Z
```diff
@@ -110,6 +110,10 @@ func applyVisibilityServerOptions(config *genericapiserver.RecommendedConfig, en
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.CertFile = certDir + "/tls.crt"
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.KeyFile = certDir + "/tls.key"
 	}
+	if kubeConfigPath != "" {
+		o.Authentication.RemoteKubeConfigFile = kubeConfigPath
```

  IIUC, it will use the custom kubeconfig.
  
  The logic in DelegatingAuthenticationOptions [getClient](https://github.com/kubernetes/apiserver/blob/b4a095b3dc1ad68dd9a775f686fa1087612ef0cc/pkg/server/options/authorization.go#L211) does the following:
  
  - Check for Remote Config File: It first checks if `len(s.RemoteKubeConfigFile) > 0`.
  - Use Custom Config: If the file path is set (which we do by assigning kubeConfigPath to RemoteKubeConfigFile), it enters the if block. Inside this block, it uses clientcmd to load the configuration specifically from that file.
  - Fallback to In-Cluster: The else block, which calls rest.InClusterConfig(), is only executed if RemoteKubeConfigFile is empty (which is what the issue is at the moment)
  
  So by passing the kubeConfigPath to `o.Authentication.RemoteKubeConfigFile` and `o.Authorization.RemoteKubeConfigFile` in applyVisibilityServerOptions, we ensure that the if condition is met.
  
  I'm not sure if that answers your question?

### Review by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) (commented) — 2026-03-04T14:13:21Z

- **cmd/kueue/main.go:142** by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-04T14:13:21Z
```diff
@@ -138,6 +136,11 @@ func main() {
 	zapOptions.BindFlags(flag.CommandLine)
 	flag.Parse()
 
+	var kubeConfigPath string
+	if kubeConfigFlag := flag.Lookup("kubeconfig"); kubeConfigFlag != nil {
+		kubeConfigPath = kubeConfigFlag.Value.String()
+	}
```

  Oh I probably misinterpreted your comment [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8761#issuecomment-3985011415). I thought you meant that extracting `--kubeconfig` explicitly would help for other purposes: `it is fair to assume values of some of the Kueue args can be by default passed to the different servers we run`. 
  
  But now I understand you are referring to the flag itself and not the extracted value.
  
  Will move the logic to `CreateAndStartVisibilityServer`

### Review by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) (commented) — 2026-03-04T14:26:25Z

- **pkg/visibility/server.go:117** by [@Nilsachy](https://github.com/Nilsachy) — 2026-03-04T14:26:25Z
```diff
@@ -110,6 +110,10 @@ func applyVisibilityServerOptions(config *genericapiserver.RecommendedConfig, en
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.CertFile = certDir + "/tls.crt"
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.KeyFile = certDir + "/tls.key"
 	}
+	if kubeConfigPath != "" {
+		o.Authentication.RemoteKubeConfigFile = kubeConfigPath
```

  I dived a bit deeper:
  
  The file path was never passed down to the visibility server's authentication and authorization options because the main controller uses `ctrl.GetConfigOrDie()` which parses the `--kubeconfig` flag and loads the configuration into a struct `(*rest.Config)`.
  
  This is passed down to the visibility server but the underlying library for the visibility server `(k8s.io/apiserver)` uses `DelegatingAuthenticationOptions`. And these options do not accept an in-memory `*rest.Config` but require a file path (as a string).
  
  So this is a mismatch between the main controller and the visibility server.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-04T14:27:36Z

- **pkg/visibility/server.go:118** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-04T14:27:36Z
```diff

 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.CertFile = certDir + "/tls.crt"
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.KeyFile = certDir + "/tls.key"
 	}
+
+	var kubeConfigPath string
+	if f := flag.Lookup("kubeconfig"); f != nil {
+		kubeConfigPath = f.Value.String()
+	}
+	if kubeConfigPath != "" {
+		o.Authentication.RemoteKubeConfigFile = kubeConfigPath
+		o.Authorization.RemoteKubeConfigFile = kubeConfigPath
```

  iiuc we can just put the two lines under `if f := flag.Lookup("kubeconfig"); f != nil {`

```diff
+func TestVisibilityServerStarts_WithCustomKubeconfig(t *testing.T) {
```

  The test looks quite complex. Could you describe its intention in the comment above? 
  
  I'm ok-ish with it, but I would like to re-consider using rather e2e tests (as suggested in the [comment](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/9619#issuecomment-4004151916) for that to avoid the tedious setup of the k8s api server mock.

### Review by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) (commented) — 2026-03-05T11:53:44Z

- **pkg/visibility/server.go:115** by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-03-05T11:53:44Z
```diff
@@ -110,6 +111,14 @@ func applyVisibilityServerOptions(config *genericapiserver.RecommendedConfig, en
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.CertFile = certDir + "/tls.crt"
 		o.SecureServing.ServerCert.CertKey.KeyFile = certDir + "/tls.key"
 	}
+
+	if f := flag.Lookup("kubeconfig"); f != nil {
```

  We are already extracting the kubeconfig for the cluster here (either from envvar or the `--kubeconfig` arg):
  https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/8491a754346bea7c50c4b099ee12fb95ef125286/cmd/kueue/main.go#L223
  It's passed to the visibility server and assigned here:
  https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/8491a754346bea7c50c4b099ee12fb95ef125286/pkg/visibility/server.go#L145
  
  Maybe instead of a flag lookup in visibility, we could pass the path as well. There is one nuance here as well, because the path of the kubeconfig returned by `GetConfigOrDie` can also be passed via an environment variable.
  
  Maybe we could have one "kubeconfig resolution" login in `main.go`, where we get both the object and it's path? And pass that downstream instead of extracting it out of the args again?

```diff
+	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/util/tlsconfig"

```

  I would be more comfortable with an e2e test which has a more "real" Kueue environment instead of one that is trying to "mock" it. It should also be simpler to write, although there might be some caveats to go around in order to make it work. 
  
  As an aside, a lot of "configuration tests" are missing anyway. For example, the [TLSOptions e2e tests](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/tree/main/keps/8190-tls-security-profiles#e2e-tests) are not implemented AFAIR. So I think this means that either:
  1. The test for this PR is optional.
  2. The test for this PR should be implemented in order to define a mechanism that will be used to test other configs (like the TLSOptions).
  
  I'd lean towards 2 unless there is some blocker.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-05T17:36:45Z

- **test/e2e/customconfigs/visibility_kubeconfig_test.go:175** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-05T17:36:46Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,193 @@
+/*
+Copyright The Kubernetes Authors.
+
+Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");
+you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.
+You may obtain a copy of the License at
+
+    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0
+
+Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software
+distributed under the License is distributed on an "AS IS" BASIS,
+WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.
+See the License for the specific language governing permissions and
+limitations under the License.
+*/
+
+package customconfigse2e
+
+import (
+	"context"
+
+	"github.com/onsi/ginkgo/v2"
+	"github.com/onsi/gomega"
+	appsv1 "k8s.io/api/apps/v1"
+	corev1 "k8s.io/api/core/v1"
+	rbacv1 "k8s.io/api/rbac/v1"
+	k8serrors "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors"
+	metav1 "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1"
+	"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client"
+
+	kueue "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/apis/kueue/v1beta2"
+	visibility "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/apis/visibility/v1beta2"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/test/util"
+)
+
+const (
+	kueueNamespace   = "kueue-system"
+	kueueManagerName = "kueue-controller-manager"
+	configMapName    = "visibility-kubeconfig-test"
+	customSAName     = "visibility-test-sa"
+	customSecretName = "visibility-test-sa-token"
+)
+
+// This kubeconfig uses the token of our custom ServiceAccount mounted at /etc/custom-sa/token.
+const rbacKubeConfig = `
+apiVersion: v1
+kind: Config
+clusters:
+- name: local
+  cluster:
+    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
+    certificate-authority: /var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt
+users:
+- name: custom-sa
+  user:
+    tokenFile: /etc/custom-sa/token
+contexts:
+- name: default
+  context:
+    cluster: local
+    user: custom-sa
+current-context: default
+`
+
+var _ = ginkgo.Describe("Visibility Server KubeConfig flag with RBAC", func() {
+	var ctx context.Context
+	var originalDeployment appsv1.Deployment
+
+	ginkgo.BeforeEach(func() {
+		ctx = context.Background()
+
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: kueueManagerName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}, &originalDeployment)
+		gomega.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+
+		// Create Custom ServiceAccount
+		sa := &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, sa))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Create a token Secret for the custom SA
+		secret := &corev1.Secret{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{
+				Name:        customSecretName,
+				Namespace:   kueueNamespace,
+				Annotations: map[string]string{corev1.ServiceAccountNameKey: customSAName},
+			},
+			Type: corev1.SecretTypeServiceAccountToken,
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, secret))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Create the ConfigMap for the KubeConfig
+		cm := &corev1.ConfigMap{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace},
+			Data:       map[string]string{"config": rbacKubeConfig},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cm))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.AfterEach(func() {
+		// Restore the original deployment
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, &originalDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		// Clean up created resources
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ConfigMap{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.Secret{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSecretName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}})
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.It("Should use the RBAC identity from the provided kubeconfig", func() {
+		patchedDeployment := originalDeployment.DeepCopy()
+
+		// Mount the ConfigMap and the Custom SA Token Secret
+		patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes = append(patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes,
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "kubeconfig-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{ConfigMap: &corev1.ConfigMapVolumeSource{LocalObjectReference: corev1.LocalObjectReference{Name: configMapName}}},
+			},
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "custom-sa-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{Secret: &corev1.SecretVolumeSource{SecretName: customSecretName}},
+			},
+		)
+
+		for i, c := range patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers {
+			if c.Name == "manager" {
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].VolumeMounts = append(c.VolumeMounts,
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "kubeconfig-vol", MountPath: "/etc/kubeconfig", ReadOnly: true},
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "custom-sa-vol", MountPath: "/etc/custom-sa", ReadOnly: true},
+				)
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].Args = append(c.Args, "--kubeconfig=/etc/kubeconfig/config")
+			}
+		}
+
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, patchedDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		cqName := "test-kubeconfig-cq"
+		cq := &kueue.ClusterQueue{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: cqName},
+			Spec:       kueue.ClusterQueueSpec{CohortName: "test-cohort"},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cq)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		defer k8sClient.Delete(ctx, cq)
+
+		// NEGATIVE TEST: The custom SA lacks 'system:auth-delegator'. The visibility server
+		// is forced to use it, so it cannot perform SubjectAccessReviews.
+		ginkgo.By("Expecting API requests to fail due to lack of auth delegation permissions")
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			var visCQ visibility.ClusterQueue
+			err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: cqName}, &visCQ)
+			g.Expect(err).To(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+			// Generally surfaces as InternalError when SAR fails
+			g.Expect(k8serrors.IsInternalError(err) || k8serrors.IsServiceUnavailable(err)).To(gomega.BeTrue())
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// POSITIVE TEST: Grant the required permissions to our custom ServiceAccount
+		ginkgo.By("Granting permissions to the custom SA and verifying requests succeed")
+		authDelegatorBinding := &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "ClusterRole", Name: "system:auth-delegator"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authDelegatorBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		authReaderBinding := &rbacv1.RoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "Role", Name: "extension-apiserver-authentication-reader"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authReaderBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Now the requests should pass successfully
```

  nit, turn the comment into ginkgo.By step for easier matching of the test output to code

```diff
+	configMapName    = "visibility-kubeconfig-test"
+	customSAName     = "visibility-test-sa"
+	customSecretName = "visibility-test-sa-token"

+
+// This kubeconfig uses the token of our custom ServiceAccount mounted at /etc/custom-sa/token.
+const rbacKubeConfig = `
+apiVersion: v1
+kind: Config
+clusters:
+- name: local
+  cluster:
+    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
+    certificate-authority: /var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt
+users:
+- name: custom-sa
+  user:
+    tokenFile: /etc/custom-sa/token
+contexts:
+- name: default
+  context:
+    cluster: local
+    user: custom-sa
+current-context: default
+`
+
+var _ = ginkgo.Describe("Visibility Server KubeConfig flag with RBAC", func() {

+	var originalDeployment appsv1.Deployment
+

+		ctx = context.Background()
+

+		gomega.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+
+		// Create Custom ServiceAccount
+		sa := &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, sa))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Create a token Secret for the custom SA
+		secret := &corev1.Secret{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{
+				Name:        customSecretName,
+				Namespace:   kueueNamespace,
+				Annotations: map[string]string{corev1.ServiceAccountNameKey: customSAName},
+			},
+			Type: corev1.SecretTypeServiceAccountToken,
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, secret))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Create the ConfigMap for the KubeConfig
+		cm := &corev1.ConfigMap{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace},
+			Data:       map[string]string{"config": rbacKubeConfig},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cm))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.AfterEach(func() {
+		// Restore the original deployment
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, &originalDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		// Clean up created resources
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ConfigMap{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.Secret{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSecretName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}})
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.It("Should use the RBAC identity from the provided kubeconfig", func() {
+		patchedDeployment := originalDeployment.DeepCopy()
+
+		// Mount the ConfigMap and the Custom SA Token Secret
+		patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes = append(patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes,
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "kubeconfig-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{ConfigMap: &corev1.ConfigMapVolumeSource{LocalObjectReference: corev1.LocalObjectReference{Name: configMapName}}},
+			},
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "custom-sa-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{Secret: &corev1.SecretVolumeSource{SecretName: customSecretName}},
+			},
+		)
+
+		for i, c := range patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers {
+			if c.Name == "manager" {
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].VolumeMounts = append(c.VolumeMounts,
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "kubeconfig-vol", MountPath: "/etc/kubeconfig", ReadOnly: true},
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "custom-sa-vol", MountPath: "/etc/custom-sa", ReadOnly: true},
+				)
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].Args = append(c.Args, "--kubeconfig=/etc/kubeconfig/config")
+			}
+		}
+
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, patchedDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		cqName := "test-kubeconfig-cq"
+		cq := &kueue.ClusterQueue{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: cqName},
+			Spec:       kueue.ClusterQueueSpec{CohortName: "test-cohort"},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cq)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		defer k8sClient.Delete(ctx, cq)
+
+		// NEGATIVE TEST: The custom SA lacks 'system:auth-delegator'. The visibility server
+		// is forced to use it, so it cannot perform SubjectAccessReviews.
+		ginkgo.By("Expecting API requests to fail due to lack of auth delegation permissions")
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			var visCQ visibility.ClusterQueue
+			err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: cqName}, &visCQ)
+			g.Expect(err).To(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+			// Generally surfaces as InternalError when SAR fails
+			g.Expect(k8serrors.IsInternalError(err) || k8serrors.IsServiceUnavailable(err)).To(gomega.BeTrue())
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// POSITIVE TEST: Grant the required permissions to our custom ServiceAccount
+		ginkgo.By("Granting permissions to the custom SA and verifying requests succeed")
+		authDelegatorBinding := &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "ClusterRole", Name: "system:auth-delegator"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authDelegatorBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		authReaderBinding := &rbacv1.RoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "Role", Name: "extension-apiserver-authentication-reader"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authReaderBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Now the requests should pass successfully
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			var visCQ visibility.ClusterQueue
+			err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: cqName}, &visCQ)
+			g.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+			g.Expect(visCQ.Name).To(gomega.Equal(cqName))
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+})
+
+func waitForDeployment(ctx context.Context, name, namespace string) {
+	gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+		var d appsv1.Deployment
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: name, Namespace: namespace}, &d)
+		g.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+		g.Expect(d.Status.UpdatedReplicas).To(gomega.Equal(d.Status.Replicas))
+		g.Expect(d.Status.ReadyReplicas).To(gomega.Equal(d.Status.Replicas))
+	}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+}
```

  Can we use `RestartKueueController` from the `e2e/util` here?

```diff
+import (
+	"context"
+
+	"github.com/onsi/ginkgo/v2"
+	"github.com/onsi/gomega"
+	appsv1 "k8s.io/api/apps/v1"
+	corev1 "k8s.io/api/core/v1"
+	rbacv1 "k8s.io/api/rbac/v1"
+	k8serrors "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors"
+	metav1 "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1"
+	"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client"
+
+	kueue "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/apis/kueue/v1beta2"

+const (
+	kueueNamespace   = "kueue-system"
+	kueueManagerName = "kueue-controller-manager"
+	configMapName    = "visibility-kubeconfig-test"
+	customSAName     = "visibility-test-sa"
+	customSecretName = "visibility-test-sa-token"
+)
+
+// This kubeconfig uses the token of our custom ServiceAccount mounted at /etc/custom-sa/token.
+const rbacKubeConfig = `
+apiVersion: v1
+kind: Config
+clusters:
+- name: local
+  cluster:
+    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
+    certificate-authority: /var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt
+users:
+- name: custom-sa
+  user:
+    tokenFile: /etc/custom-sa/token
+contexts:
+- name: default
+  context:
+    cluster: local
+    user: custom-sa
+current-context: default
+`
+
+var _ = ginkgo.Describe("Visibility Server KubeConfig flag with RBAC", func() {
+	var ctx context.Context
+	var originalDeployment appsv1.Deployment
+
+	ginkgo.BeforeEach(func() {
+		ctx = context.Background()
+
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: kueueManagerName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}, &originalDeployment)
+		gomega.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+
+		// Create Custom ServiceAccount
+		sa := &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, sa))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Create a token Secret for the custom SA
+		secret := &corev1.Secret{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{
+				Name:        customSecretName,
+				Namespace:   kueueNamespace,
+				Annotations: map[string]string{corev1.ServiceAccountNameKey: customSAName},
+			},
+			Type: corev1.SecretTypeServiceAccountToken,
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, secret))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Create the ConfigMap for the KubeConfig
+		cm := &corev1.ConfigMap{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace},
+			Data:       map[string]string{"config": rbacKubeConfig},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cm))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.AfterEach(func() {
+		// Restore the original deployment
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, &originalDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		// Clean up created resources
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ConfigMap{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.Secret{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSecretName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}})
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.It("Should use the RBAC identity from the provided kubeconfig", func() {
+		patchedDeployment := originalDeployment.DeepCopy()
+
+		// Mount the ConfigMap and the Custom SA Token Secret
+		patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes = append(patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes,
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "kubeconfig-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{ConfigMap: &corev1.ConfigMapVolumeSource{LocalObjectReference: corev1.LocalObjectReference{Name: configMapName}}},
+			},
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "custom-sa-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{Secret: &corev1.SecretVolumeSource{SecretName: customSecretName}},
+			},
+		)
+
+		for i, c := range patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers {
+			if c.Name == "manager" {
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].VolumeMounts = append(c.VolumeMounts,
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "kubeconfig-vol", MountPath: "/etc/kubeconfig", ReadOnly: true},
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "custom-sa-vol", MountPath: "/etc/custom-sa", ReadOnly: true},
+				)
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].Args = append(c.Args, "--kubeconfig=/etc/kubeconfig/config")
+			}
+		}
+
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, patchedDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		cqName := "test-kubeconfig-cq"
+		cq := &kueue.ClusterQueue{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: cqName},
+			Spec:       kueue.ClusterQueueSpec{CohortName: "test-cohort"},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cq)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		defer k8sClient.Delete(ctx, cq)
+
+		// NEGATIVE TEST: The custom SA lacks 'system:auth-delegator'. The visibility server
+		// is forced to use it, so it cannot perform SubjectAccessReviews.
+		ginkgo.By("Expecting API requests to fail due to lack of auth delegation permissions")
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			var visCQ visibility.ClusterQueue
+			err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: cqName}, &visCQ)
+			g.Expect(err).To(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+			// Generally surfaces as InternalError when SAR fails
+			g.Expect(k8serrors.IsInternalError(err) || k8serrors.IsServiceUnavailable(err)).To(gomega.BeTrue())
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// POSITIVE TEST: Grant the required permissions to our custom ServiceAccount
+		ginkgo.By("Granting permissions to the custom SA and verifying requests succeed")
+		authDelegatorBinding := &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "ClusterRole", Name: "system:auth-delegator"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authDelegatorBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		authReaderBinding := &rbacv1.RoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "Role", Name: "extension-apiserver-authentication-reader"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authReaderBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Now the requests should pass successfully
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			var visCQ visibility.ClusterQueue
+			err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: cqName}, &visCQ)

+			g.Expect(visCQ.Name).To(gomega.Equal(cqName))
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+})
+
+func waitForDeployment(ctx context.Context, name, namespace string) {
+	gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+		var d appsv1.Deployment
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: name, Namespace: namespace}, &d)
+		g.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())

+		g.Expect(d.Status.ReadyReplicas).To(gomega.Equal(d.Status.Replicas))
+	}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+}
```

  Sorry, I meant `WaitForKueueAvailabilityNoRestartCountCheck` since changing the deployment spec already restarts it.

```diff
+    cluster: local
+    user: custom-sa

+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, sa))).To(gomega.Succeed())

+		secret := &corev1.Secret{

+				Namespace:   kueueNamespace,
+				Annotations: map[string]string{corev1.ServiceAccountNameKey: customSAName},
+			},
+			Type: corev1.SecretTypeServiceAccountToken,
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, secret))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Create the ConfigMap for the KubeConfig
+		cm := &corev1.ConfigMap{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace},
+			Data:       map[string]string{"config": rbacKubeConfig},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cm))).To(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.AfterEach(func() {
+		// Restore the original deployment
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, &originalDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		// Clean up created resources
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ConfigMap{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.Secret{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSecretName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"}})
+		_ = k8sClient.Delete(ctx, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}})
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.It("Should use the RBAC identity from the provided kubeconfig", func() {
+		patchedDeployment := originalDeployment.DeepCopy()
+
+		// Mount the ConfigMap and the Custom SA Token Secret
+		patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes = append(patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes,
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "kubeconfig-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{ConfigMap: &corev1.ConfigMapVolumeSource{LocalObjectReference: corev1.LocalObjectReference{Name: configMapName}}},
+			},
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "custom-sa-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{Secret: &corev1.SecretVolumeSource{SecretName: customSecretName}},
+			},
+		)
+
+		for i, c := range patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers {
+			if c.Name == "manager" {
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].VolumeMounts = append(c.VolumeMounts,
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "kubeconfig-vol", MountPath: "/etc/kubeconfig", ReadOnly: true},
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "custom-sa-vol", MountPath: "/etc/custom-sa", ReadOnly: true},
+				)
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].Args = append(c.Args, "--kubeconfig=/etc/kubeconfig/config")
+			}
+		}
+
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, patchedDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		waitForDeployment(ctx, kueueManagerName, kueueNamespace)
+
+		cqName := "test-kubeconfig-cq"
+		cq := &kueue.ClusterQueue{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: cqName},
+			Spec:       kueue.ClusterQueueSpec{CohortName: "test-cohort"},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, cq)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		defer k8sClient.Delete(ctx, cq)
+
+		// NEGATIVE TEST: The custom SA lacks 'system:auth-delegator'. The visibility server
+		// is forced to use it, so it cannot perform SubjectAccessReviews.
+		ginkgo.By("Expecting API requests to fail due to lack of auth delegation permissions")
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			var visCQ visibility.ClusterQueue
+			err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: cqName}, &visCQ)
+			g.Expect(err).To(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+			// Generally surfaces as InternalError when SAR fails
+			g.Expect(k8serrors.IsInternalError(err) || k8serrors.IsServiceUnavailable(err)).To(gomega.BeTrue())
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// POSITIVE TEST: Grant the required permissions to our custom ServiceAccount
+		ginkgo.By("Granting permissions to the custom SA and verifying requests succeed")
+		authDelegatorBinding := &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "ClusterRole", Name: "system:auth-delegator"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authDelegatorBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		authReaderBinding := &rbacv1.RoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "Role", Name: "extension-apiserver-authentication-reader"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Create(ctx, authReaderBinding)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// Now the requests should pass successfully
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			var visCQ visibility.ClusterQueue
+			err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: cqName}, &visCQ)
+			g.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+			g.Expect(visCQ.Name).To(gomega.Equal(cqName))
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+})
+
+func waitForDeployment(ctx context.Context, name, namespace string) {
+	gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+		var d appsv1.Deployment
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: name, Namespace: namespace}, &d)
+		g.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+		g.Expect(d.Status.UpdatedReplicas).To(gomega.Equal(d.Status.Replicas))
+		g.Expect(d.Status.ReadyReplicas).To(gomega.Equal(d.Status.Replicas))
+	}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+}
```

  Yes, let's reuse the preexisting functions. Waiting for availability is surprisingly tricky, especially in the context of restart, because sometimes traffic may keep reaching the terminating replicas as the Endpoints contain the old endpoints. So, it took as a while to fix some corner cases there.

- **test/e2e/customconfigs/visibility_kubeconfig_test.go:225** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-06T18:18:15Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,249 @@
+/*

+package customconfigse2e
+
+import (
+	"context"
+
+	"github.com/onsi/ginkgo/v2"
+	"github.com/onsi/gomega"
+	appsv1 "k8s.io/api/apps/v1"
+	corev1 "k8s.io/api/core/v1"
+	rbacv1 "k8s.io/api/rbac/v1"
+	k8serrors "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors"
+	metav1 "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1"
+	"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client"
+
+	kueue "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/apis/kueue/v1beta2"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/test/util"
+)
+
+const (
+	kueueNamespace   = "kueue-system"
+	kueueManagerName = "kueue-controller-manager"
+	configMapName    = "visibility-kubeconfig-test"
+	customSAName     = "visibility-test-sa"
+	customSecretName = "visibility-test-sa-token"
+	testLabelKey     = "visibility-test-rbac"
+	testLabelValue   = "true"
+)
+
+// This kubeconfig uses the token of our custom ServiceAccount mounted at /etc/custom-sa/token.
+const rbacKubeConfig = `
+apiVersion: v1
+kind: Config
+clusters:
+- name: local
+  cluster:
+    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
+    certificate-authority: /var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt
+users:
+- name: custom-sa
+  user:
+    tokenFile: /etc/custom-sa/token
+contexts:
+- name: default
+  context:
+    cluster: local
+    user: custom-sa
+current-context: default
+`
+
+var _ = ginkgo.Describe("Visibility Server KubeConfig flag with RBAC", func() {
+	var ctx context.Context
+	var originalDeployment appsv1.Deployment
+
+	ginkgo.BeforeEach(func() {
+		ctx = context.Background()
+
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: kueueManagerName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}, &originalDeployment)
+		gomega.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+
+		// Create Custom ServiceAccount
+		sa := &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, sa)
+
+		// Create a token Secret for the custom SA
+		secret := &corev1.Secret{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{
+				Name:        customSecretName,
+				Namespace:   kueueNamespace,
+				Annotations: map[string]string{corev1.ServiceAccountNameKey: customSAName},
+			},
+			Type: corev1.SecretTypeServiceAccountToken,
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, secret)
+
+		// Create the ConfigMap for the KubeConfig
+		cm := &corev1.ConfigMap{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace},
+			Data:       map[string]string{"config": rbacKubeConfig},
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, cm)
+
+		// Clone all base permissions to our custom SA so the main controller can boot,
+		// explicitly holding back the auth delegation permission for our negative test.
+		cloneControllerRBAC(ctx)
+
+		// Create the auth-reader binding so the visibility server can start up.
+		authReaderBinding := &rbacv1.RoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "Role", Name: "extension-apiserver-authentication-reader"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, authReaderBinding)
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.AfterEach(func() {
+		// Restore the original deployment
+		latestDeployment := &appsv1.Deployment{}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Get(ctx, client.ObjectKeyFromObject(&originalDeployment), latestDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		latestDeployment.Spec = originalDeployment.Spec
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, latestDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		util.WaitForKueueAvailabilityNoRestartCountCheck(ctx, k8sClient)
+
+		// Clean up created resources
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &corev1.ConfigMap{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &corev1.Secret{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSecretName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}}, true)
+
+		// Clean up our dynamically cloned roles
+		_ = k8sClient.DeleteAllOf(ctx, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{}, client.MatchingLabels{testLabelKey: testLabelValue})
+		_ = k8sClient.DeleteAllOf(ctx, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{}, client.InNamespace(kueueNamespace), client.MatchingLabels{testLabelKey: testLabelValue})
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.It("Should use the RBAC identity from the provided kubeconfig", func() {
+		patchedDeployment := originalDeployment.DeepCopy()
+
+		// Mount the ConfigMap and the Custom SA Token Secret
+		patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes = append(patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes,
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "kubeconfig-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{ConfigMap: &corev1.ConfigMapVolumeSource{LocalObjectReference: corev1.LocalObjectReference{Name: configMapName}}},
+			},
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "custom-sa-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{Secret: &corev1.SecretVolumeSource{SecretName: customSecretName}},
+			},
+		)
+
+		for i, c := range patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers {
+			if c.Name == "manager" {
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].VolumeMounts = append(c.VolumeMounts,
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "kubeconfig-vol", MountPath: "/etc/kubeconfig", ReadOnly: true},
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "custom-sa-vol", MountPath: "/etc/custom-sa", ReadOnly: true},
+				)
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].Args = append(c.Args, "--kubeconfig=/etc/kubeconfig/config")
+			}
+		}
+
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, patchedDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		util.WaitForKueueAvailabilityNoRestartCountCheck(ctx, k8sClient)
+
+		cqName := "test-kubeconfig-cq"
+		cq := &kueue.ClusterQueue{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: cqName},
+			Spec:       kueue.ClusterQueueSpec{CohortName: "test-cohort"},
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, cq)
+		defer util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, cq, true)
+
+		// NEGATIVE TEST: The custom SA lacks 'system:auth-delegator'. The visibility server
+		// is forced to use it, so it cannot perform SubjectAccessReviews.
+		ginkgo.By("Expecting API requests to fail due to lack of auth delegation permissions")
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			visClient := util.CreateVisibilityClient("")
+			_, err := visClient.ClusterQueues().GetPendingWorkloadsSummary(ctx, cqName, metav1.GetOptions{})
+			g.Expect(err).To(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+
+			// Check for standard auth failures (401/403) or generic server errors (500/503)
+			isExpectedError := k8serrors.IsUnauthorized(err) ||
+				k8serrors.IsForbidden(err) ||
+				k8serrors.IsInternalError(err) ||
+				k8serrors.IsServiceUnavailable(err)
+
+			g.Expect(isExpectedError).To(gomega.BeTrue(), "Expected an auth or internal error, but got: %v", err)
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		// POSITIVE TEST: Grant the required permissions to our custom ServiceAccount
+		ginkgo.By("Granting permissions to the custom SA and verifying requests succeed")
+		authDelegatorBinding := &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "ClusterRole", Name: "system:auth-delegator"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, authDelegatorBinding)
+
+		ginkgo.By("Now the requests should pass successfully")
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			visClient := util.CreateVisibilityClient("")
+			pw, err := visClient.ClusterQueues().GetPendingWorkloadsSummary(ctx, cqName, metav1.GetOptions{})
+			g.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+			g.Expect(pw).NotTo(gomega.BeNil())
+		}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+})
+
+// cloneControllerRBAC dynamically copies all RoleBindings and ClusterRoleBindings
+// from the default Kueue SA to our custom SA, explicitly omitting system:auth-delegator.
+func cloneControllerRBAC(ctx context.Context) {
+	// Clone ClusterRoleBindings
+	var crbs rbacv1.ClusterRoleBindingList
+	gomega.Expect(k8sClient.List(ctx, &crbs)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+	for _, crb := range crbs.Items {
+		for _, sub := range crb.Subjects {
+			if sub.Kind == "ServiceAccount" && sub.Name == "kueue-controller-manager" && sub.Namespace == kueueNamespace {
+				// Skip the roles that grant SubjectAccessReview permissions
+				if crb.RoleRef.Name == "system:auth-delegator" || crb.RoleRef.Name == "kueue-metrics-auth-role" {
+					continue
+				}
+				newCRB := &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{
+					ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{
+						Name:   "vistest-copy-" + crb.Name,
+						Labels: map[string]string{testLabelKey: testLabelValue},
+					},
+					RoleRef:  crb.RoleRef,
+					Subjects: []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+				}
+				_ = client.IgnoreAlreadyExists(k8sClient.Create(ctx, newCRB))
```

  why would that already exist? If becuase of the previous test run, then instead of them please make sure the test cleans after itself.

- **test/e2e/customconfigs/visibility_kubeconfig_test.go:105** by [@dkaluza](https://github.com/dkaluza) — 2026-03-09T09:33:53Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,249 @@
+/*
+Copyright The Kubernetes Authors.
+
+Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");
+you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.
+You may obtain a copy of the License at
+

+WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.
+See the License for the specific language governing permissions and
+limitations under the License.
+*/
+
+package customconfigse2e
+
+import (
+	"context"
+
+	"github.com/onsi/ginkgo/v2"
+	"github.com/onsi/gomega"
+	appsv1 "k8s.io/api/apps/v1"
+	corev1 "k8s.io/api/core/v1"
+	rbacv1 "k8s.io/api/rbac/v1"
+	k8serrors "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors"
+	metav1 "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1"
+	"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client"
+
+	kueue "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/apis/kueue/v1beta2"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/test/util"
+)
+
+const (
+	kueueNamespace   = "kueue-system"
+	kueueManagerName = "kueue-controller-manager"
+	configMapName    = "visibility-kubeconfig-test"
+	customSAName     = "visibility-test-sa"
+	customSecretName = "visibility-test-sa-token"
+	testLabelKey     = "visibility-test-rbac"
+	testLabelValue   = "true"
+)
+
+// This kubeconfig uses the token of our custom ServiceAccount mounted at /etc/custom-sa/token.
+const rbacKubeConfig = `
```

```diff
+	testLabelValue   = "true"

+kind: Config

+- name: local
+  cluster:
+    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
+    certificate-authority: /var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt

+contexts:
+- name: default
+  context:
+    cluster: local
+    user: custom-sa
+current-context: default
+`
+

+	var ctx context.Context
+	var originalDeployment appsv1.Deployment
+
+	ginkgo.BeforeEach(func() {
+		ctx = context.Background()
+
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: kueueManagerName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}, &originalDeployment)
+		gomega.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())

+
```

```diff
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}}, true)
```

```diff
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}}, true)
+
+		// Clean up our dynamically cloned roles
+		_ = k8sClient.DeleteAllOf(ctx, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{}, client.MatchingLabels{testLabelKey: testLabelValue})
+		_ = k8sClient.DeleteAllOf(ctx, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{}, client.InNamespace(kueueNamespace), client.MatchingLabels{testLabelKey: testLabelValue})
+	})

+	ginkgo.It("Should use the RBAC identity from the provided kubeconfig", func() {
+		patchedDeployment := originalDeployment.DeepCopy()
+
+		// Mount the ConfigMap and the Custom SA Token Secret
+		patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes = append(patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes,
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "kubeconfig-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{ConfigMap: &corev1.ConfigMapVolumeSource{LocalObjectReference: corev1.LocalObjectReference{Name: configMapName}}},
+			},
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "custom-sa-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{Secret: &corev1.SecretVolumeSource{SecretName: customSecretName}},
+			},
+		)
+

+			if c.Name == "manager" {
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].VolumeMounts = append(c.VolumeMounts,
```

```diff
+
+package customconfigse2e
+
+import (
+	"context"
+
+	"github.com/onsi/ginkgo/v2"
+	"github.com/onsi/gomega"
+	appsv1 "k8s.io/api/apps/v1"
+	corev1 "k8s.io/api/core/v1"
+	rbacv1 "k8s.io/api/rbac/v1"
+	k8serrors "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors"
+	metav1 "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1"
+	"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client"
+
+	kueue "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/apis/kueue/v1beta2"
+	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/test/util"
+)
+
+const (
+	kueueNamespace   = "kueue-system"
+	kueueManagerName = "kueue-controller-manager"
+	configMapName    = "visibility-kubeconfig-test"
+	customSAName     = "visibility-test-sa"
+	customSecretName = "visibility-test-sa-token"
+	testLabelKey     = "visibility-test-rbac"
+	testLabelValue   = "true"
+)
+
+// This kubeconfig uses the token of our custom ServiceAccount mounted at /etc/custom-sa/token.
+const rbacKubeConfig = `
+apiVersion: v1
+kind: Config
+clusters:
+- name: local
+  cluster:
+    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
+    certificate-authority: /var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt
+users:
+- name: custom-sa
+  user:
+    tokenFile: /etc/custom-sa/token
+contexts:
+- name: default
+  context:
+    cluster: local
+    user: custom-sa
+current-context: default
+`
+
+var _ = ginkgo.Describe("Visibility Server KubeConfig flag with RBAC", func() {
+	var ctx context.Context
+	var originalDeployment appsv1.Deployment
+
+	ginkgo.BeforeEach(func() {
+		ctx = context.Background()
+
+		err := k8sClient.Get(ctx, types.NamespacedName{Name: kueueManagerName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}, &originalDeployment)
+		gomega.Expect(err).NotTo(gomega.HaveOccurred())
+
+		// Create Custom ServiceAccount
+		sa := &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, sa)
+
+		// Create a token Secret for the custom SA
+		secret := &corev1.Secret{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{
+				Name:        customSecretName,
+				Namespace:   kueueNamespace,
+				Annotations: map[string]string{corev1.ServiceAccountNameKey: customSAName},
+			},
+			Type: corev1.SecretTypeServiceAccountToken,
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, secret)
+
+		// Create the ConfigMap for the KubeConfig
+		cm := &corev1.ConfigMap{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace},
+			Data:       map[string]string{"config": rbacKubeConfig},
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, cm)
+
+		// Clone all base permissions to our custom SA so the main controller can boot,
+		// explicitly holding back the auth delegation permission for our negative test.
+		cloneControllerRBAC(ctx)
+
+		// Create the auth-reader binding so the visibility server can start up.
+		authReaderBinding := &rbacv1.RoleBinding{
+			ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"},
+			RoleRef:    rbacv1.RoleRef{APIGroup: "rbac.authorization.k8s.io", Kind: "Role", Name: "extension-apiserver-authentication-reader"},
+			Subjects:   []rbacv1.Subject{{Kind: "ServiceAccount", Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}},
+		}
+		util.MustCreate(ctx, k8sClient, authReaderBinding)
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.AfterEach(func() {
+		// Restore the original deployment
+		latestDeployment := &appsv1.Deployment{}
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Get(ctx, client.ObjectKeyFromObject(&originalDeployment), latestDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		latestDeployment.Spec = originalDeployment.Spec
+		gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, latestDeployment)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		util.WaitForKueueAvailabilityNoRestartCountCheck(ctx, k8sClient)
+
+		// Clean up created resources
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &corev1.ConfigMap{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: configMapName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &corev1.Secret{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSecretName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &corev1.ServiceAccount{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: customSAName, Namespace: kueueNamespace}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-delegator"}}, true)
+		util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(ctx, k8sClient, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: "visibility-test-auth-reader", Namespace: "kube-system"}}, true)
+
+		// Clean up our dynamically cloned roles
+		_ = k8sClient.DeleteAllOf(ctx, &rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding{}, client.MatchingLabels{testLabelKey: testLabelValue})
+		_ = k8sClient.DeleteAllOf(ctx, &rbacv1.RoleBinding{}, client.InNamespace(kueueNamespace), client.MatchingLabels{testLabelKey: testLabelValue})
+	})
+
+	ginkgo.It("Should use the RBAC identity from the provided kubeconfig", func() {
+		patchedDeployment := originalDeployment.DeepCopy()
+
+		// Mount the ConfigMap and the Custom SA Token Secret
+		patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes = append(patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Volumes,
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "kubeconfig-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{ConfigMap: &corev1.ConfigMapVolumeSource{LocalObjectReference: corev1.LocalObjectReference{Name: configMapName}}},
+			},
+			corev1.Volume{
+				Name:         "custom-sa-vol",
+				VolumeSource: corev1.VolumeSource{Secret: &corev1.SecretVolumeSource{SecretName: customSecretName}},
+			},
+		)
+
+		for i, c := range patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers {
+			if c.Name == "manager" {
+				patchedDeployment.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[i].VolumeMounts = append(c.VolumeMounts,
+					corev1.VolumeMount{Name: "kubeconfig-vol", MountPath: "/etc/kubeconfig", ReadOnly: true},
```

  Consider consts for volume names to make sure they are always consistent with template spec volumes
